## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (batch reactor / concentration-time ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is an instantaneous reaction rate expressed as the time derivative of concentration A(t), which is the standard formulation of chemical kinetics in well-mixed (0D) systems. With only (t, A) available, the most common structures are rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, autocatalysis, equilibrium relaxation) and possibly explicit time-dependence to represent changing conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited or saturated regime over a range)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition, pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction or second-order in A approximation)
- General n-th order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/unknown reaction order fit)
- Parallel pathways (sum of orders): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (coexisting unimolecular and bimolecular loss channels)
- Competing production and consumption: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant feed/source with first-order removal; CSTR-like lumped form)
- Reversible/relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (linear approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic growth/decay term: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (self-enhancing at low A with self-limitation at higher A; simplified autocatalysis)
- General polynomial kinetics: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (lumped empirical kinetics capturing multiple mechanisms near an operating range)
- Time-varying first-order rate coefficient (exponential): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (decreasing effective rate due to catalyst deactivation or condition drift)
- Time-varying first-order rate coefficient (linear ramp): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * t) * A (rate changing approximately linearly in time due to protocol changes)
- Nonlinear relaxation (higher-order restoring): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) - c2 * (A - c1)**3 (near-equilibrium kinetics with nonlinear corrections)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is predominantly negative and proportional to A, the system is likely first-order (straight line when plotting dA_dt vs A).
- If dA_dt scales with A**2 (curvature in dA_dt vs A), it suggests bimolecular/self-reaction behavior or second-order loss dominance.
- A sum of multiple powers of A (e.g., A and A**2 terms) often indicates parallel reaction pathways contributing additively to the net rate.
- Presence of a constant term in dA_dt (nonzero rate at AŌēł0) indicates an external source/sink independent of A (feed, background generation, or baseline loss).
- A factor (A - c1) indicates relaxation toward an equilibrium/steady concentration c1; the sign of (A - c1) determines whether A increases or decreases.
- Explicit time dependence in the rate coefficient (e.g., exp(-c*t) or (1+c*t)) suggests changing operating conditions (catalyst aging, mixing/temperature program) not captured by A alone.
- A cubic (A - c1)**3 correction commonly captures asymmetric/nonlinear restoring behavior near equilibrium, hinting at non-idealities or higher-order steps.
- Net-growth-at-low-A but net-decay-at-high-A (e.g., c*A - c*A**2) indicates self-accelerating kinetics with self-limitation, consistent with autocatalysis or resource-limited regimes.

\[
f(t,A)= -kA -kA e^{-\lambda t} + s\sin(\log(A+1))
\]
with \(k=0.2566735\), \(\lambda=0.02053594\), \(s=0.9426404\).  
Key structural requirements (up to domain restriction like \(A\ge 0\)):  
1) exactly two linear-in-\(A\) terms: one constant coefficient \((-kA)\) and one with a decaying exponential in \(t\) \((-kA e^{-\lambda t})\).  
2) an additive sine of a log in \(A\): \(\sin(\log(A+1))\) (no \(t\) inside sine; amplitude constant).  
3) no extra dependence like \(A^2\), \(1/|A|\), \(\log(\cdot)\) outside sine, etc., unless their coefficients can be set to 0.

Now check candidates.
